### PROMPT
> We want to be able to create an episode from an iOS shortcut. This should be achievable by using a curl command to the API endpoint.\n\nRight now we have the following API endpoint:\n- POST /episodes: to upload a youtube video url and download the audio file.\n\nThis endpoint should be protected by an API key used by our frontend. \n\nUsers should be able to use the shortcut to create an episode from a youtube video url by hitting the share button in the youtube app and selecting the Labcastarr shortcut which will just execute the curl command to the API endpoint. We should simplify the workflow and make it as simple as possible for the user. Should we have just one dedicated api endpoint to create an episode from a youtube video url without any token authentication? Is there any other way to achieve this goal but retaining some security measures?\n\nWhat would be the best approach to create an iOS shortcut that can be used to create an episode from a youtube video url?\n

### RESULT
```


I'll analyze your current API setup and design the best approach for an iOS Shortcut integration that balances simplicity with security.
I'll analyze your current API setup and design the best approach for an iOS Shortcut integration that balances simplicity with security.

вЏє Read(/Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/backend/app/core/config.py)

вЏє Read(/Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env.production)

I'll analyze your current API setup and design the best approach for an iOS Shortcut integration that balances simplicity with security.

вЏє Grep()


Now I have a comprehensive understanding of your setup. Let me analyze the best approaches for iOS Shortcut integration.

## Analysis & Recommendations

Based on my review of your codebase, here are the key findings and recommendations:

### Current State
1. **Existing Authentication**: Your API uses `X-API-Key` header authentication via `API_KEY_SECRET` environment variable
2. **Episode Creation Endpoint**: `POST /v1/episodes` - currently has NO authentication dependency in the code
3. **API Key Configuration**: 
   - Development: `QnNz9ad73MhjIe2/lV/i+XG8TFbeN+b2q0GfJ6buDig=`
   - Production: Different key in production
4. **Router Structure**: No global API key middleware applied - each endpoint would need individual protection

### Security Options for iOS Shortcut

I recommend **Option 2** (see plan below) - a dedicated shortcut-friendly endpoint with simplified API key auth. Here's why each option works:

#### Option 1: Use Existing Endpoint with API Key (Simple but Less Secure)
**Pros:**
- No code changes needed
- Works immediately
- Users just add header to shortcut

**Cons:**
- Exposes your main API key on iOS device
- If key is compromised, entire API is vulnerable
- No ability to revoke shortcut access separately

#### Option 2: Dedicated Shortcut Endpoint with Separate API Key (Recommended)
**Pros:**
- Separate authentication scope (revoke shortcut access without affecting frontend)
- Can add rate limiting specific to shortcuts
- Can track/audit shortcut usage separately
- Simple for users (just one API key to configure)
- More secure isolation

**Cons:**
- Requires minimal code changes
- Need to manage additional API key

#### Option 3: User-Specific API Keys (Most Secure)
**Pros:**
- Each user gets their own API key
- Full auditability per user
- Can revoke individual user access
- Best security practice

**Cons:**
- More complex implementation
- Users need to generate/manage their own keys
- Requires user management system updates

### iOS Shortcut Implementation

The shortcut would be extremely simple with any option:

```bash
# Basic curl command structure
curl -X POST "https://labcastarr-api.oliverbarreto.com/v1/shortcuts/episode" \
  -H "X-Shortcut-Key: <user-key-here>" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{
    "video_url": "SHORTCUT_INPUT_URL",
    "channel_id": 1
  }'
```

The iOS Shortcut would:
1. Receive YouTube URL from Share Sheet
2. Make HTTP POST request with the URL
3. Show success/failure notification

вЏє ExitPlanMode()

- Separate authentication scope (revoke shortcut access without affecting frontend)
- Can add rate limiting specific to shortcuts
- Can track/audit shortcut usage separately
- Simple for users (just one API key to configure)
- More secure isolation

**Cons:**
- Requires minimal code changes
- Need to manage additional API key

#### Option 3: User-Specific API Keys (Most Secure)
**Pros:**
- Each user gets their own API key
- Full auditability per user
- Can revoke individual user access
- Best security practice

**Cons:**
- More complex implementation
- Users need to generate/manage their own keys
- Requires user management system updates

### iOS Shortcut Implementation

The shortcut would be extremely simple with any option:

```bash
# Basic curl command structure
curl -X POST "https://labcastarr-api.oliverbarreto.com/v1/shortcuts/episode" \
  -H "X-Shortcut-Key: <user-key-here>" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{
    "video_url": "SHORTCUT_INPUT_URL",
    "channel_id": 1
  }'
```

The iOS Shortcut would:
1. Receive YouTube URL from Share Sheet
2. Make HTTP POST request with the URL
3. Show success/failure notification

## Analysis & Recommendations

Based on my review of your codebase, here are the key findings and recommendations:

### Current State
1. **Existing Authentication**: Your API uses `X-API-Key` header authentication via `API_KEY_SECRET` environment variable
2. **Episode Creation Endpoint**: `POST /v1/episodes` - currently has NO authentication dependency in the code
3. **API Key Configuration**: 
   - Development: `QnNz9ad73MhjIe2/lV/i+XG8TFbeN+b2q0GfJ6buDig=`
   - Production: Different key in production
4. **Router Structure**: No global API key middleware applied - each endpoint would need individual protection

### Security Options for iOS Shortcut

I recommend **Option 2** (see plan below) - a dedicated shortcut-friendly endpoint with simplified API key auth. Here's why each option works:

#### Option 1: Use Existing Endpoint with API Key (Simple but Less Secure)
**Pros:**
- No code changes needed
- Works immediately
- Users just add header to shortcut

**Cons:**
- Exposes your main API key on iOS device
- If key is compromised, entire API is vulnerable
- No ability to revoke shortcut access separately

#### Option 2: Dedicated Shortcut Endpoint with Separate API Key (Recommended)
**Pros:**
- Separate authentication scope (revoke shortcut access without affecting frontend)
- Can add rate limiting specific to shortcuts
- Can track/audit shortcut usage separately
- Simple for users (just one API key to configure)
- More secure isolation

**Cons:**
- Requires minimal code changes
- Need to manage additional API key

#### Option 3: User-Specific API Keys (Most Secure)
**Pros:**
- Each user gets their own API key
- Full auditability per user
- Can revoke individual user access
- Best security practice

**Cons:**
- More complex implementation
- Users need to generate/manage their own keys
- Requires user management system updates
